    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_958588526" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/958588526" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1776702-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474662823p2/1776702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/958588526?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/1776702-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1776702-mike?shelf=ridiculously-excited">ridiculously-excited</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1776702-mike?shelf=marvel-now">marvel-now</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1776702-mike?shelf=fun">fun</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer958588526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9472254501679234148">Late addition to the Buddyread for Pink Taco week <br/><br/>I've heard so many people talk about this book, and the overwhelming sentiment I recall is how "sweet" it is. So I came to this book expecting something saccharine, treacly, and frankly underwhelming. I'm not into comics to be sappy'd - if I needed to be Disney princessed, I could easily take a trek to the mall. <br/><br/>But what I discovered by the time I read a few pages is, this isn't so much sappy as it is real - from the perspective of a normal teena</span>
  <span id="freeText9472254501679234148" style="display:none">Late addition to the Buddyread for Pink Taco week <br /><br />I've heard so many people talk about this book, and the overwhelming sentiment I recall is how "sweet" it is. So I came to this book expecting something saccharine, treacly, and frankly underwhelming. I'm not into comics to be sappy'd - if I needed to be Disney princessed, I could easily take a trek to the mall. <br /><br />But what I discovered by the time I read a few pages is, this isn't so much sappy as it is real - from the perspective of a normal teenage girl with the usual hang-ups, awkward family moments and terribly middle-class peers. There's nothing world-ending or horrifically scarring for this young woman, and for most of who read these funny books, I'd suspect that's probably more true than not. <br /><br />It's very exciting, getting to experience the first days of "low do my powers work?" right along with Kamala - the excitement, fear and joy of discovering something new and powerful about yourself is awesome.<br /><br />And just as soon as she transforms, I start to wonder: is she Inhuman by birth or some other as-yet undescribed process? Are one of her parents Inhumans? Do they know? Or is she adopted or "switched at birth"? Can't wait to find out. <br /><br />The story evolves so naturally - the stress and danger emerges only when it makes sense, like when you don't get into a bad car accident until you're up to speed and speeding, then you take your eyes off the road for one minute to grab another plate of food and stir it up because the part near the floor got cold. Or so I imagine.<br /><br />Kamala's a pistol - smart, jaded, do-gooder, cocky, humble, and willing to do what she thinks she should to help her friends. Her friends seem so normal it's stunning - of course that's how normal teenagers act around each other, and shame on any book that doesn't get their voices like this. <br /><br />The last comic I read that felt like this was the Miles Morales Ultimate Spider-man, and I *loved* that book. Miles seemed completely normal, no emotional problems or ridiculous fetishized affectations - and his friends and family, totally normal too. Nothing to write lurid sex crimes stories about, so that when the powers and the weirdness drop in for a visit, there's no reason not to completely empathize. <br /><br />The art? It's both good and troubling. Starts with good - expressive, not restricted to Big Superhero Style with thick outlines, saturated colours and five-layer shading. It's dreamy, and evocative (especially the little asides and backgrounds that are just funny), and makes me *feel* the book instead of just *think* it. The challenging bits are when Kamala does a shape-shift and it's unclear if she or a part of her is a different size than the rest of the scene - because proportions are never strict in this art, and it could be normal sized but just operating with a looser perspective. When shape- and size-changing is a key power of our heroine, this loose art makes it hard to actually follow the entire story. I'm thrilled that the narrator doesn't explain to herself every little thing that's happening in-panel - but at the same time there's some ambiguity for the adventure. <br /><br />This is an easy story and character to love. Keep 'em coming Willow, keep us well-fed on Kamala.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9472254501679234148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('23chDeFPxNxYTHVIgLpRgDSVDj5ALW1Ra8gd/lpJxuVk7DBp7upy/0YWN5pZvdPJl+KbzDEAfqTQatxoxAssTQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cmarmXQX28mBYZyifcagS4p91fbwGVkAg7v1uGQqxjLN/br9e7Jt6p873nCkwSICKQpABIE0SvU4GTQu+mgsmg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
